<p>The <b>Mongol Empire</b> (<a href="/wiki/Mongolian_language" title="Mongolian language">Mongolian</a>: <i>Mongolyn Ezent Güren</i> <span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Mongoliinezentguren.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e4/Mongoliinezentguren.ogg" title="Mongoliinezentguren.ogg">listen</a></span> <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Mongoliinezentguren.ogg" title="File:Mongoliinezentguren.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>; <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Mongolian Cyrillic alphabet">Mongolian Cyrillic</a>: Монголын эзэнт гүрэн; <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Mongolian" title="Help:IPA for Mongolian">[mɔŋɡ(ɔ)ɮˈiːŋ ɛt͡sˈɛnt ˈɡurəŋ]</a></span>; also <span lang="ru" xml:lang="ru">Орда</span> ("Horde") in <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Russian</a> <a href="/wiki/Complete_Collection_of_Russian_Chronicles" title="Complete Collection of Russian Chronicles">chronicles</a>) existed during the 13th and 14th centuries and was the largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires#Largest_empires_by_land_area_and_population" title="List of largest empires">contiguous land empire</a> in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[2]</a></sup> Originating in the <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppes</a> of <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, the Mongol Empire eventually stretched from <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">Sea of Japan</a>, extending northwards into <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, eastwards and southwards into the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indochina" title="Indochina">Indochina</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iranian_plateau" title="Iranian plateau">Iranian plateau</a>, and westwards as far as the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabia</a>.</p>
<p>The Mongol Empire emerged from the unification of nomadic tribes in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol" title="Mongol">Mongol</a> homeland under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a>, who was proclaimed ruler of all Mongols in 1206. The empire grew rapidly under the rule of him and his descendants, who sent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions" title="Mongol invasions">invasions</a> in every direction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[4]</a></sup> The vast transcontinental empire connected the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">east</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">west</a> with an enforced <i><a href="/wiki/Pax_Mongolica" title="Pax Mongolica">Pax Mongolica</a></i> allowing trade, technologies, commodities, and ideologies to be disseminated and exchanged across <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The empire began to split due to wars over succession, as the grandchildren of Genghis Khan disputed whether the royal line should follow from his son and initial heir <a href="/wiki/%C3%96gedei_Khan" title="Ögedei Khan">Ögedei</a> or one of his other sons, such as <a href="/wiki/Tolui" title="Tolui">Tolui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khan" title="Chagatai Khan">Chagatai</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Jochi" title="Jochi">Jochi</a>. The Toluids prevailed after a bloody purge of Ögedeid and Chagataid factions, but disputes continued even among the descendants of Tolui. After <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6ngke_Khan" title="Möngke Khan">Möngke Khan</a> died, rival <a href="/wiki/Kurultai" title="Kurultai">kurultai</a> councils simultaneously elected different successors, the brothers <a href="/wiki/Ariq_B%C3%B6ke" title="Ariq Böke">Ariq Böke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a>, who then not only fought each other in the <a href="/wiki/Toluid_Civil_War" title="Toluid Civil War">Toluid Civil War</a>, but also dealt with challenges from descendants of other sons of Genghis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[8]</a></sup> Kublai successfully took power, but civil war ensued as Kublai sought unsuccessfully to regain control of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chagatai_khans" title="Chagatai khans">Chagatayid</a> and <a href="/wiki/House_of_%C3%96gedei" title="House of Ögedei">Ögedeid</a> families.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ain_Jalut" title="Battle of Ain Jalut">Battle of Ain Jalut</a> in 1260 marked the high point of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_conquests" title="Mongol conquests">Mongol conquests</a> and was the first time a Mongol advance had ever been beaten back in direct combat on the battlefield. Though the Mongols launched many more invasions on the Levant, briefly occupying it and raiding as far as <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Gaza" title="Gaza">Gaza</a> after a decisive victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wadi_al-Khazandar" title="Battle of Wadi al-Khazandar">Battle of Wadi al-Khazandar</a> in 1299, they withdrew due to various geopolitical factors.</p>
<p>By the time of <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai's</a> death in 1294, the Mongol Empire had <a href="/wiki/Division_of_the_Mongol_Empire" title="Division of the Mongol Empire">fractured into four separate khanates or empires</a>, each pursuing its own separate interests and objectives: the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a> khanate in the northwest; the <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khanate" title="Chagatai Khanate">Chagatai Khanate</a> in the middle; the <a href="/wiki/Ilkhanate" title="Ilkhanate">Ilkhanate</a> in the southwest; and the <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a> in the east based in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China_p413_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-China_p413-12">[9]</a></sup> In 1304, the three western khanates briefly accepted the nominal <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a> of the Yuan dynasty,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[11]</a></sup> but it was later overthrown by the <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a> <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> in 1368. The Genghisid rulers of the Yuan retreated to the Mongolia homeland and continued to rule the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Yuan_dynasty" title="Northern Yuan dynasty">Northern Yuan dynasty</a>, while the Golden Horde and the Chagatai Khanate lasted in one form or another for some additional centuries after the fall of the Yuan dynasty and the Ilkhanate.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>What is referred to in English as the Mongol Empire was called the <b>Ikh Mongol Uls</b> (<i>ikh</i>: great, <i>uls</i>: state; Great Mongolian State).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[12]</a></sup> In the 1240s, one of Genghis's descendants, <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Khan" title="Güyük Khan">Güyük Khan</a>, wrote a letter to <a href="/wiki/Pope_Innocent_IV" title="Pope Innocent IV">Pope Innocent IV</a> which used the preamble "Dalai (great/oceanic) Khagan of the great Mongolian state (ulus)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the succession war between <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a> and his brother <a href="/wiki/Ariq_B%C3%B6ke" title="Ariq Böke">Ariq Böke</a>, Ariq limited Kublai's power to the eastern part of the empire. Kublai officially issued an imperial <a href="/wiki/Edict" title="Edict">edict</a> on December 18, 1271 to name the country "Great Yuan" (<i>Dai Yuan</i>, or <i>Dai Ön Ulus</i>) to establish the <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a>. Some sources state that the full Mongolian name was <i>Dai Ön Yehe Monggul Ulus</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-empire_context">Pre-empire context</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-empire context">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Proto-Mongols" title="Proto-Mongols">Proto-Mongols</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mongolia_XI.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="523" data-file-width="830" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Mongolia_XI.jpg/250px-Mongolia_XI.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Mongolia_XI.jpg/375px-Mongolia_XI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Mongolia_XI.jpg/500px-Mongolia_XI.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mongolia_XI.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mongolian tribes during the Khitan <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao dynasty</a> (907-1125)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:East-Hem_1200ad.jpg"><img alt="Map of Eurasia showing the different states" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1903" data-file-width="3240" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/East-Hem_1200ad.jpg/250px-East-Hem_1200ad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/East-Hem_1200ad.jpg/375px-East-Hem_1200ad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/East-Hem_1200ad.jpg/500px-East-Hem_1200ad.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:East-Hem_1200ad.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> on the eve of the Mongol invasions, <i>c.</i> 1200.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The area around <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a>, and parts of <a href="/wiki/North_China" title="North China">North China</a> had been controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao dynasty</a> since the 10th century. In 1125, the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115–1234)">Jin dynasty</a> founded by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jurchens" title="Jurchens">Jurchens</a> overthrew the Liao dynasty and attempted to gain control over former Liao territory in Mongolia. In the 1130s the Jin dynasty rulers, known as the Golden Kings, successfully resisted the <a href="/wiki/Khamag_Mongol" title="Khamag Mongol">Khamag Mongol</a> confederation, ruled at the time by <a href="/wiki/Khabul_Khan" title="Khabul Khan">Khabul Khan</a>, great grandfather of Temujin (Genghis Khan).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barfield._p._184_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barfield._p._184-18">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongolian_plateau" title="Mongolian plateau">Mongolian plateau</a> was occupied mainly by five powerful tribal confederations (<i>khanlig</i>): <a href="/wiki/Keraites" title="Keraites">Keraites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khamag_Mongol" title="Khamag Mongol">Khamag Mongol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naimans" title="Naimans">Naiman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merkit" title="Merkit">Mergid</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tatar_confederation" title="Tatar confederation">Tatar</a>. The Jin emperors, following a policy of <a href="/wiki/Divide_and_rule" title="Divide and rule">divide and rule</a>, encouraged disputes among the tribes, especially between the Tatars and Mongols, in order to keep the nomadic tribes distracted by their own battles and thereby away from the Jin. Khabul's successor was <a href="/wiki/Ambaghai" title="Ambaghai">Ambaghai Khan</a>, who was betrayed by the Tatars, handed over to the Jurchen, and executed. The Mongols retaliated by raiding the frontier, resulting in a failed Jurchen counter-attack in 1143.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barfield._p._184_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barfield._p._184-18">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1147, the Jin somewhat changed their policy, signing a peace treaty with the Mongols and withdrawing a score of forts. The Mongols then resumed attacks on the Tatars to avenge the death of their late khan, opening a long period of active hostilities. The Jin and Tatar armies defeated the Mongols in 1161.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barfield._p._184_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-Barfield._p._184-18">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the rise of the Mongol Empire in the 13th century, the usually cold, parched steppes of central Asia enjoyed their mildest, wettest conditions in more than a millennium. It is thought that as a result, a rapid increase in the number of war horses and other livestock significantly enhanced Mongol military strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_of_Genghis_Khan">Rise of Genghis Khan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Rise of Genghis Khan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Khamag_Mongol" title="Khamag Mongol">Khamag Mongol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg"><img alt="Painting of Genghis Khan" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1016" data-file-width="793" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg/220px-YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg/330px-YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg/440px-YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_Museum" title="National Palace Museum">National Palace Museum</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taipei,_Taiwan" title="Taipei, Taiwan">Taipei, Taiwan</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Known during his childhood as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temujin" title="Temujin">Temujin</a>, Genghis Khan was the son of a Mongol chieftain. When his young wife <a href="/wiki/B%C3%B6rte" title="Börte">Börte</a> was kidnapped by a rival tribe, Temujin united the nomadic, previously ever-rivaling Mongol tribes under his rule through political manipulation and military might. His most powerful allies were his father's friend, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khereid" title="Khereid">Khereid</a> chieftain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wang_Khan" title="Wang Khan">Wang Khan</a> Toghoril, and Temujin's childhood <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anda_(Mongol)" title="Anda (Mongol)"><i>anda</i></a> (friend) <a href="/wiki/Jamukha" title="Jamukha">Jamukha</a> of the Jadran clan. With their help, Temujin defeated the Merkit tribe, rescued his wife Börte, and went on to defeat the Naimans and Tatars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morgan-49_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-morgan-49-20">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Temujin forbade looting of his enemies without permission, and he implemented a policy of sharing spoils with his Mongol warriors and their families instead of giving it all to the aristocrats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[18]</a></sup> He thus held the Khan title. These policies brought him into conflict with his uncles, who were also legitimate heirs to the throne; they regarded Temujin not as leader but merely an insolent usurper. This controversy spread to his generals and other associates, and some Mongols who had previously been allies with him broke their allegiance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morgan-49_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-morgan-49-20">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>War ensued, and Temujin and the forces still loyal to him prevailed, destroying all the remaining rival tribes from 1203 to 1205 and bringing them under his sway. In 1206, Temujin was crowned as the <a href="/wiki/Khagan" title="Khagan">khagan</a> of the <i>Yekhe Mongol Ulus</i> (Great Mongol State) at a <a href="/wiki/Kurultai" title="Kurultai">kurultai</a> (general assembly/council). It was there that he assumed the title of Genghis Khan (universal leader) instead of one of the old tribal titles such as Gur Khan or Tayang Khan, marking the start of the Mongol Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morgan-49_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-morgan-49-20">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_organization">Early organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3088" data-file-width="2823" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg/220px-Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg/330px-Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg/440px-Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a> ascended the throne in the Yeke Quriltay region in the Onan river, from the <a href="/wiki/Jami%27_al-tawarikh" title="Jami' al-tawarikh">Jami' al-tawarikh</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Genghis Khan introduced many innovative ways of organizing his army, dividing it into decimal subsections of arbans (10 people), zuuns (100), <a href="/wiki/Mingghan" title="Mingghan">Mingghans</a> (1000), and <a href="/wiki/Tumen_(unit)" title="Tumen (unit)">tumens</a> (10,000). The <a href="/wiki/Kheshig" title="Kheshig">Kheshig</a>, or the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_guard" title="Imperial guard">imperial guard</a>, was founded and divided into day (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khorchin" title="Khorchin">khorchin</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torghuds" title="Torghuds">torghuds</a>) and night guards (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khevtuul" title="Khevtuul">khevtuul</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[19]</a></sup> Genghis rewarded those who had been loyal to him and placed them in high positions, placing them as heads of army units and households, even though many of his allies had been from very low-rank clans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Secret_history._p._203_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Secret_history._p._203-23">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Compared to the units he gave to his loyal companions, those assigned to his own family members were quite few. He proclaimed a new law of the empire, Ikh Zasag or <a href="/wiki/Yassa" title="Yassa">Yassa</a>, and codified everything related to the everyday life and political affairs of the nomads at the time. He forbade the selling of women, theft of other's properties, fighting among the Mongols, and the hunting of animals during the breeding season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Secret_history._p._203_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Secret_history._p._203-23">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>He appointed his adopted brother Shigi-Khuthugh supreme judge (jarughachi), ordering him to keep records of the empire. In addition to laws regarding family, food, and the army, Genghis also decreed religious freedom and supported domestic and international trade. He exempted the poor and the clergy from taxation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[21]</a></sup> He also encouraged literacy, adopting the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uyghur_script" title="Uyghur script">Uyghur script</a>, which would form the <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_script" title="Mongolian script">Uyghur-Mongolian script</a> of the empire, and he ordered the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uyghur_people" title="Uyghur people">Uyghur</a> Tatatunga, who had previously served the khan of Naimans, to instruct his sons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Push_into_Central_Asia">Push into Central Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Push into Central Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Central_Asia" title="Mongol invasion of Central Asia">Mongol invasion of Central Asia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="532" data-file-width="813" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png/220px-Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png/330px-Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png/440px-Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mongol Empire circa 1207</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Genghis quickly came into conflict with the Jin dynasty of the Jurchens and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Xia" title="Western Xia">Western Xia</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tanguts" title="Tanguts">Tanguts</a> in northern China. He also had to deal with two other powers, Tibet and Khara Khitai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[23]</a></sup> Towards the west he moved into <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, devastating <a href="/wiki/Transoxiana" title="Transoxiana">Transoxiana</a> and eastern Persia, then raiding into <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Kievan Rus'</a> (a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Predecessor_state" title="Predecessor state">predecessor state</a> of Russia, <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morgan-49_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-morgan-49-20">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before his death, Genghis Khan divided his empire among his sons and immediate family, making the Mongol Empire the joint property of the entire imperial family who, along with the Mongol aristocracy, constituted the ruling class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_policies">Religious policies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Religious policies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Genghis Khan and the following Yuan emperors forbade Islamic practices like Halal butchering, forcing Muslims to comply with Mongol methods of butchering animals, and other restrictive decrees continued. Muslims had to slaughter sheep in secret.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[25]</a></sup> Genghis Khan directly called Muslims and Jews "slaves", and demanded that they follow the Mongol method of eating rather than the halal method. <a href="/wiki/Circumcision" title="Circumcision">Circumcision</a> was also forbidden. Jews were also affected, and forbidden by the Mongols to eat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kosher" title="Kosher">kosher</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[26]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>Among all the [subject] alien peoples only the Hui-hui say “we do not eat Mongol food”. [Cinggis Qa’an replied:] “By the aid of heaven we have pacified you; you are our slaves. Yet you do not eat our food or drink. How can this be right?” He thereupon made them eat. “If you slaughter sheep, you will be considered guilty of a crime.” He issued a regulation to that effect ... [In 1279/1280 under Qubilai] all the Muslims say: “if someone else slaughters [the animal] we do not eat”. Because the poor people are upset by this, from now on, Musuluman [Muslim] Huihui and Zhuhu [Jewish] Huihui, no matter who kills [the animal] will eat [it] and must cease slaughtering sheep themselves, and cease the rite of circumcision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[27]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Genghis Khan arranged for the Chinese Daoist master <a href="/wiki/Qiu_Chuji" title="Qiu Chuji">Qiu Chuji</a> to visit him in Afghanistan and put him in charge of all religious affairs in the empire.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_Genghis_Khan_and_expansion_under_.C3.96gedei_.281227.E2.80.931241.29">Death of Genghis Khan and expansion under Ögedei (1227–1241)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Death of Genghis Khan and expansion under Ögedei (1227–1241)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_and_conquests" title="Mongol invasions and conquests">Mongol invasions and conquests</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2006" data-file-width="1420" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg/220px-CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg/330px-CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg/440px-CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Coronation of <a href="/wiki/%C3%96gedei_Khan" title="Ögedei Khan">Ögedei Khan</a> in 1229 as the successor of Genghis Khan. By <a href="/wiki/Rashid-al-Din_Hamadani" title="Rashid-al-Din Hamadani">Rashid al-Din</a>, early 14th century.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Genghis Khan died on August 18, 1227, by which time the Mongol Empire ruled from the Pacific Ocean to the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> — an empire twice the size of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> and Muslim <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Caliphate</a>. Genghis named his third son, the charismatic <a href="/wiki/%C3%96gedei_Khan" title="Ögedei Khan">Ögedei</a>, as his heir. According to Mongol tradition, Genghis Khan was buried in a secret location. The regency was originally held by Ögedei's younger brother <a href="/wiki/Tolui" title="Tolui">Tolui</a> until Ögedei's formal election at the kurultai in 1229.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Among his first actions, Ögedei sent troops to subjugate the <a href="/wiki/Bashkirs" title="Bashkirs">Bashkirs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a>, and other nations in the Kipchak-controlled steppes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[29]</a></sup> In the east, Ögedei's armies re-established Mongol authority in Manchuria, crushing the <a href="/wiki/Puxian_Wannu" title="Puxian Wannu">Eastern Xia</a> regime and <a href="/wiki/Tungusic_peoples" title="Tungusic peoples">Water Tatars</a>. In 1230, the great khan personally led his army in the campaign against the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115–1234)">Jin dynasty</a> (China). Ögedei's general <a href="/wiki/Subutai" title="Subutai">Subutai</a> captured the capital of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Aizong_of_Jin" title="Emperor Aizong of Jin">Wanyan Shouxu</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_siege_of_Kaifeng" title="Mongol siege of Kaifeng">siege of Kaifeng</a> in 1232.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[30]</a></sup> The Jin dynasty collapsed in 1234 when the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Caizhou" title="Siege of Caizhou">Mongols captured Caizhou</a>, the town where Wanyan Shouxu had fled. In 1234, three armies commanded by Ögedei's sons Kochu and Koten, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Tangut_people" title="Tangut people">Tangut</a> general Chagan, invaded southern China. With the assistance of the <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a>, the Mongols finished off the Jin in 1234.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many Han Chinese and Khitan defected to the Mongols to fight against the Jin. Two Han Chinese leaders, <a href="/wiki/Shi_Tianze" title="Shi Tianze">Shi Tianze</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Liu_Heima&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Liu Heima (page does not exist)">Liu Heima</a> (劉黑馬, Liu Ni),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[33]</a></sup> and the Khitan <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Xiao_Zhala&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Xiao Zhala (page does not exist)">Xiao Zhala</a> defected and commanded the 3 Tumens in the Mongol army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup> Liu Heima and Shi Tianze served Ogödei Khan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup> Liu Heima and Shi Tianxiang led armies against Western Xia for the Mongols.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[36]</a></sup> There were four Han Tumens and three Khitan Tumens, with each Tumen consisting of 10,000 troops.</p>
<p>Shi Tianze was a Han Chinese who lived in the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115–1234)">Jin dynasty (1115–1234)</a>. Interethnic marriage between Han and Jurchen became common at this time. His father was Shi Bingzhi (史秉直, Shih Ping-chih). Shi Bingzhi was married to a Jurchen woman (surname Na-ho) and a Han Chinese woman (surname Chang). It is unknown which of them was Shi Tianze's mother.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ed._de_Rachewiltz_1993_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-ed._de_Rachewiltz_1993-40">[37]</a></sup> Shi Tianze was married to two Jurchen women, a Han Chinese woman, and a Korean woman, and his son Shi Gang was born to one of his Jurchen wives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[38]</a></sup> His Jurchen wive's surnames were Mo-nien and Na-ho, his Korean wife's surname was Li, and his Han Chinese wife's surname was Shi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ed._de_Rachewiltz_1993_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-ed._de_Rachewiltz_1993-40">[37]</a></sup> Shi Tianze defected to the Mongol Empire's forces upon <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_the_Jin_dynasty" title="Mongol conquest of the Jin dynasty">their invasion of the Jin dynasty</a>. His son Shi Gang married a Kerait woman. The Kerait were Mongolified Turkic people and considered part of the Mongol nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Yuan dynasty created a Han army 漢軍 out of defected Jin troops and army of defected Song troops called the Newly Submitted Army 新附軍.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the West, Ögedei's general <a href="/wiki/Chormaqan" title="Chormaqan">Chormaqan</a> destroyed <a href="/wiki/Jalal_ad-Din_Mingburnu" title="Jalal ad-Din Mingburnu">Jalal ad-Din Mingburnu</a>, the last <a href="/wiki/Shah" title="Shah">shah</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Khwarazmian_dynasty" title="Khwarazmian dynasty">Khwarizmian Empire</a>. The small kingdoms in Southern Persia voluntarily accepted Mongol supremacy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[43]</a></sup> In East Asia, there were a number of <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Korea" title="Mongol invasions of Korea">Mongolian campaigns into Goryeo Korea</a>, but Ögedei's attempt to annex the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Peninsula" title="Korean Peninsula">Korean Peninsula</a> met with little success. <a href="/wiki/Gojong_of_Goryeo" title="Gojong of Goryeo">Gojong</a>, the king of <a href="/wiki/Goryeo" title="Goryeo">Goryeo</a>, surrendered but later revolted and massacred Mongol <i><a href="/wiki/Darughachi" title="Darughachi">darughachis</a></i> (overseers); he then moved his imperial court from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaeseong" title="Gaeseong">Gaeseong</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ganghwa_Island" title="Ganghwa Island">Ganghwa Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the empire grew, Ögedei established a Mongol capital at <a href="/wiki/Karakorum" title="Karakorum">Karakorum</a> in northwestern Mongolia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Invasions_of_Kievan_Rus.27_and_central_China">Invasions of Kievan Rus' and central China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Invasions of Kievan Rus' and central China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Rus%27" title="Mongol invasion of Rus'">Mongol invasion of Rus'</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_China" title="Mongol invasion of China">Mongol invasion of China</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_India" title="Mongol invasions of India">Mongol invasions of India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Korea" title="Mongol invasions of Korea">Mongol invasions of Korea</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_Tibet" title="Mongol conquest of Tibet">Mongol conquest of Tibet</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg"><img alt="Painting of a battle scene" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="926" data-file-width="694" height="294" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg/220px-Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg/330px-Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg/440px-Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The sack of <a href="/wiki/Suzdal" title="Suzdal">Suzdal</a> by <a href="/wiki/Batu_Khan" title="Batu Khan">Batu Khan</a> in 1238, <a href="/wiki/Miniature_(illuminated_manuscript)" title="Miniature (illuminated manuscript)">miniature</a> from 16th-century chronicle</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Meanwhile, in an offensive action against the <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a>, Mongol armies captured Siyang-yang, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sichuan" title="Sichuan">Sichuan</a>, but did not secure their control over the conquered sites. The Song generals were able to recapture Siyang-yang from the Mongols in 1239. After the sudden death of Ögedei's son Kochu in Chinese territory, the Mongols withdrew from southern China, although Kochu's brother Prince Koten invaded <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a> right after their withdrawal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morgan-49_20-4"><a href="#cite_note-morgan-49-20">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Batu_Khan" title="Batu Khan">Batu Khan</a>, another grandson of Genghis Khan, overran the countries of the <a href="/wiki/Volga_Bulgaria" title="Volga Bulgaria">Bulgars</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a>, the Kypchaks, Bashkirs, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mordvin" title="Mordvin">Mordvins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chuvash_people" title="Chuvash people">Chuvash</a>, and other nations of the southern <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Steppe#Russian_Steppe" title="Eurasian Steppe">Russian steppe</a>. By 1237, the Mongols began encroaching upon <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Ryazan" title="Principality of Ryazan">Ryazan</a>, their first <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Kievan Rus'</a> principality. After a three-day siege using heavy attacks, the Mongols captured the city and massacred its inhabitants, then proceeded to destroy the army of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_principality_of_Vladimir" title="Grand principality of Vladimir">Grand principality of Vladimir</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Sit_River" title="Battle of the Sit River">Battle of the Sit River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Timothy_May._Chormaqan._p._32_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Timothy_May._Chormaqan._p._32-49">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Mongols captured the <a href="/wiki/Alania" title="Alania">Alania</a> capital <a href="/wiki/Maghas" title="Maghas">Maghas</a> in 1238. By 1240, all Kievan Rus' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Kievan_Rus%27" title="Mongol invasion of Kievan Rus'">had fallen to the Asian invaders</a> except for a few northern cities. Mongol troops under Chormaqan in Persia <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Georgia_and_Armenia" title="Mongol invasions of Georgia and Armenia">connected his invasion</a> of <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasia</a> with the invasion of Batu and Subutai, forced the <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenian</a> nobles to surrender as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Timothy_May._Chormaqan._p._32_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-Timothy_May._Chormaqan._p._32-49">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giovanni_de_Plano_Carpini" title="Giovanni de Plano Carpini">Giovanni de Plano Carpini</a>, the pope's envoy to the Mongol great khan, traveled through <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a> in February 1246 and wrote:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>They [the Mongols] attacked Russia, where they made great havoc, destroying cities and fortresses and slaughtering men; and they laid siege to Kiev, the capital of Russia; after they had besieged the city for a long time, they took it and put the inhabitants to death. When we were journeying through that land we came across countless skulls and bones of dead men lying about on the ground. Kiev had been a very large and thickly populated town, but now it has been reduced almost to nothing, for there are at the present time scarce two hundred houses there and the inhabitants are kept in complete slavery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[47]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Despite the military successes, strife continued within the Mongol ranks. Batu's relations with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G%C3%BCy%C3%BCk" title="Güyük">Güyük</a>, Ögedei's eldest son, and <a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCri" title="Büri">Büri</a>, the beloved grandson of <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khan" title="Chagatai Khan">Chagatai Khan</a>, remained tense and worsened during Batu's victory banquet in southern Kievan Rus'. Nevertheless, Güyük and Buri could not do anything to harm Batu's position as long as his uncle Ögedei was still alive. Meanwhile, Ögedei continued with <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_India" title="Mongol invasions of India">invasions into the Indian subcontinent</a>, temporarily investing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uchch" title="Uchch">Uchch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lahore" title="Lahore">Lahore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Multan" title="Multan">Multan</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Sultanate" title="Delhi Sultanate">Delhi Sultanate</a> and stationing a Mongol overseer in <a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">Kashmir</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[48]</a></sup> though the invasions into India eventually failed and were forced to retreat. In northeastern Asia, Ögedei agreed to settle conflicts with <a href="/wiki/Goryeo" title="Goryeo">Goryeo</a> by making it a client state and sent Mongolian princesses to wed Goryeo princes. He then reinforced his keshig with the Koreans through both diplomacy and military force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Push_into_central_Europe">Push into central Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Push into central Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Europe" title="Mongol invasion of Europe">Mongol invasion of Europe</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Legnica.JPG"><img alt="Painting of a battle scene with mounted warriors on either side" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="632" data-file-width="886" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Legnica.JPG/220px-Legnica.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Legnica.JPG/330px-Legnica.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Legnica.JPG/440px-Legnica.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Legnica.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Legnica" title="Battle of Legnica">battle of Liegnitz</a>, 1241. From a medieval manuscript of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hedwig_of_Poland" title="Hedwig of Poland">Hedwig</a> legend.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Europe" title="Mongol invasion of Europe">advance into Europe</a> continued with Mongol invasions of Poland and Hungary. When the western flank of the Mongols plundered Polish cities, a European alliance among the <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravians</a>, and the Christian military orders of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hospitallers" title="Hospitallers">Hospitallers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teutonic_Knights" title="Teutonic Knights">Teutonic Knights</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Templar" title="Knights Templar">Templars</a> assembled sufficient forces to halt, although briefly, the Mongol advance <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Legnica" title="Battle of Legnica">at Legnica</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Hungarian</a> army, their <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croatian allies</a> and the Templar Knights were beaten by Mongols at the banks of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mohi" title="Battle of Mohi">Sajo River</a> on April 11, 1241. After their victories over European knights at <a href="/wiki/Legnica" title="Legnica">Legnica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muhi" title="Muhi">Muhi</a>, Mongol armies quickly advanced across <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babenberg" title="Babenberg">Babenberg</a> Austria and then into the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before Batu's forces could continue into <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> and northern <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, news of Ögedei's death in December 1241 brought a halt to the invasion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weatherford._p._158_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weatherford._p._158-57">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[55]</a></sup> As was customary in Mongol military tradition, all princes of Genghis's line had to attend the kurultai to elect a successor. Batu and his western Mongol army withdrew from Central Europe the next year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._p._104_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._p._104-59">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-.C3.96gedei_power_struggles_.281241.E2.80.931251.29">Post-Ögedei power struggles (1241–1251)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Post-Ögedei power struggles (1241–1251)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the Great Khan Ögedei's death in 1241, and before the next kurultai, Ögedei's widow <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T%C3%B6regene" title="Töregene">Töregene</a> took over the empire. She persecuted her husband's Khitan and Muslim officials, giving high positions to her own allies. She built palaces, cathedrals, and social structures on an imperial scale, supporting religion and education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson._p._95_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson._p._95-60">[57]</a></sup> She was able to win over most Mongol aristocrats to support Ögedei's son <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Khan" title="Güyük Khan">Güyük</a>. But Batu, ruler of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a>, refused to come to the kurultai, claiming that he was ill and that the Mongolian climate was too harsh for him. The resulting stalemate lasted more than four years and further destabilized the unity of the empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson._p._95_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson._p._95-60">[57]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A6%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%96.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="220" data-file-width="282" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/%D0%A6%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%96.jpg/220px-%D0%A6%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%96.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/88/%D0%A6%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%96.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A6%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%96.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Batu_Khan" title="Batu Khan">Batu Khan</a> consolidates the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>When Genghis Khan's youngest brother <a href="/wiki/Tem%C3%BCge" title="Temüge">Temüge</a> threatened Töregene to seize the throne, Güyük came to Karakorum to try to secure his position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[58]</a></sup> Batu eventually agreed to send his brothers and generals to the kurultai convened by Töregene in 1246. Güyük by this time was ill and alcoholic, but his campaigns in Manchuria and Europe gave him the kind of stature necessary for a great khan. He was duly elected at a ceremony attended by Mongols and foreign dignitaries from both within and without the empire — leaders of vassal nations, representatives from Rome, and other entities who came to the kurultai to show their respects and negotiate diplomacy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2593" data-file-width="495" height="524" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg/100px-LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg/150px-LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg/200px-LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Khan" title="Güyük Khan">Güyük Khan</a> demanding <a href="/wiki/Pope_Innocent_IV" title="Pope Innocent IV">Pope Innocent IV</a>'s submission. The letter was written in <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Güyük took steps to reduce corruption, announcing that he would continue the policies of his father Ögedei, not Töregene. He punished Töregene's supporters except governor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arghun_the_Elder" title="Arghun the Elder">Arghun the Elder</a>. He also replaced young <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qara_H%C3%BCl%C3%ABg%C3%BC" title="Qara Hülëgü">Qara Hülëgü</a>, the khan of the <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khanate" title="Chagatai Khanate">Chagatai Khanate</a>, with his favorite cousin <a href="/wiki/Yes%C3%BC_M%C3%B6ngke" title="Yesü Möngke">Yesü Möngke</a> to assert his newly conferred powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atwood-255_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-atwood-255-64">[61]</a></sup> He restored his father's officials to their former positions and was surrounded by the Uyghur, <a href="/wiki/Naimans" title="Naimans">Naiman</a>, and Central Asian officials, favoring <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a> commanders who helped his father conquer Northern China. He continued military operations in Korea, advanced into Song China in the south and Iraq in the west, and ordered an empire-wide census. Güyük also divided the Sultanate of Rum between <a href="/wiki/Kaykaus_II" title="Kaykaus II">Izz-ad-Din Kaykawus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kilij_Arslan_IV" title="Kilij Arslan IV">Rukn ad-Din Kilij Arslan</a>, though Kaykawus disagreed with this decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atwood-255_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-atwood-255-64">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Not all parts of the empire respected Güyük's election. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hashshashin" title="Hashshashin">Hashshashins</a>, former Mongol allies whose Grand Master Hasan Jalalud-Din had offered his submission to Genghis Khan in 1221, angered Güyük by refusing to submit. He instead murdered Mongol generals in Persia. Güyük appointed his best friend's father <a href="/wiki/Eljigidei" title="Eljigidei">Eljigidei</a> as chief commander of the troops in Persia and gave them the task of both reducing the strongholds of the <a href="/wiki/Assassins" title="Assassins">Assassins</a> Muslim movement and conquering the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasids" title="Abbasids">Abbasids</a> in the center of the Islamic world, Iran and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atwood-255_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-atwood-255-64">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_G.C3.BCy.C3.BCk_.281248.29">Death of Güyük (1248)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Death of Güyük (1248)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 1248, Güyük raised more troops and suddenly marched westwards from the Mongol capital of Karakorum. The reasoning was unclear. Some sources wrote that he sought to recuperate his personal property Emyl; others suggested that he might have been moving to join Eljigidei to conduct a full-scale conquest of the Middle East or possibly to make a surprise attack on his rival cousin Batu Khan in Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atwood._p._213_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Atwood._p._213-67">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Suspicious of Güyük's motives, <a href="/wiki/Sorghaghtani_Beki" title="Sorghaghtani Beki">Sorghaghtani Beki</a>, the widow of Genghis's son Tolui, secretly warned her nephew Batu of Güyük's approach. Batu had himself been traveling eastwards at the time, possibly to pay homage, or perhaps with other plans in mind. Before the forces of Batu and Güyük met, Güyük, sick and worn out by travel, died en route at Qum-Senggir (Hong-siang-yi-eulh) in <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a>, possibly a victim of poison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atwood._p._213_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-Atwood._p._213-67">[64]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Turtle-Karakorum.jpg"><img alt="Photograph of a field with a large stone tortoise" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="392" data-file-width="500" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Turtle-Karakorum.jpg/220px-Turtle-Karakorum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Turtle-Karakorum.jpg/330px-Turtle-Karakorum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Turtle-Karakorum.jpg/440px-Turtle-Karakorum.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Turtle-Karakorum.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Stone_Turtle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Stone Turtle (page does not exist)">Stone Turtle</a> at the site of the Mongol capital, <a href="/wiki/Karakorum" title="Karakorum">Karakorum</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Güyük's widow <a href="/wiki/Oghul_Qaimish" title="Oghul Qaimish">Oghul Qaimish</a> stepped forward to take control of the empire, but she lacked the skills of her mother-in-law Töregene, and her young sons Khoja and Naku and other princes challenged her authority. To decide on a new great khan, Batu called a kurultai on his own territory in 1250. As it was far from the Mongolian heartland, members of the Ögedeid and Chagataid families refused to attend. The kurultai offered the throne to Batu, but he rejected it, claiming he had no interest in the position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._159_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._159-68">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Batu instead nominated <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6ngke_Khan" title="Möngke Khan">Möngke</a>, a grandson of Genghis from his son Tolui's lineage. Möngke was leading a Mongol army in Russia, the Northern Caucasus, and Hungary. The pro-Tolui faction rose up and supported Batu's choice, and Möngke was elected, though given the kurultai's limited attendance and location, it was of questionable validity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._159_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._159-68">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Batu sent Möngke under the protection of his brothers, <a href="/wiki/Berke" title="Berke">Berke</a> and Tukhtemur, and his son <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sartaq" title="Sartaq">Sartaq</a> to assemble a more formal kurultai at Kodoe Aral in the heartland. The supporters of Möngke invited Oghul Qaimish and other main Ögedeid and Chagataid princes to attend the kurultai, but they refused each time. The Ögedeid and Chagataid princes refused to accept a descendant of Genghis's son Tolui as leader, demanding that only descendants of Genghis's son Ögedei could be great khan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._159_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._159-68">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rule_of_M.C3.B6ngke_Khan_.281251.E2.80.931259.29">Rule of Möngke Khan (1251–1259)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rule of Möngke Khan (1251–1259)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When Möngke's mother Sorghaghtani and their cousin <a href="/wiki/Berke" title="Berke">Berke</a> organized a second kurultai on July 1, 1251, the assembled throng proclaimed Möngke great khan of the Mongol Empire. This marked a major shift in the leadership of the empire, transferring power from the descendants of Genghis's son Ögedei to the descendants of Genghis's son Tolui. The decision was acknowledged by a few of the Ögedeid and Chagataid princes, such as Möngke's cousin <a href="/wiki/Kadan" title="Kadan">Kadan</a> and the deposed khan Qara Hülëgü, but one of the other legitimate heirs, Ögedei's grandson Shiremun, sought to topple Möngke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._pp._103_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._pp._103-69">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shiremun moved with his own forces towards the emperor's nomadic palace with a plan for an armed attack, but Möngke was alerted by his falconer of the plan. Möngke ordered an investigation of the plot, which led to a series of major trials all across the empire. Many members of the Mongol elite were found guilty and put to death, with estimates ranging from 77–300, though princes of Genghis's royal line were often exiled rather than executed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._pp._103_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._pp._103-69">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Möngke eliminated the estates of the Ögedeid and the Chagatai families and shared the western part of the empire with his ally <a href="/wiki/Batu_Khan" title="Batu Khan">Batu Khan</a>. After the bloody purge, Möngke ordered a general amnesty for prisoners and captives, but thereafter the power of the great khan's throne remained firmly with the descendants of Genghis's son Tolui.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._pp._103_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._pp._103-69">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_reforms">Administrative reforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Administrative reforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Möngke was a serious man who followed the laws of his ancestors and avoided alcoholism. He was tolerant of outside religions and artistic styles, leading to the building of foreign merchants' quarters, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist_monasteries" title="Buddhist monasteries">Buddhist monasteries</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mosques" title="Mosques">mosques</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian_churches" title="Christian churches">Christian churches</a> in the Mongol capital. As construction projects continued, Karakorum was adorned with Chinese, European, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persian_architecture" title="Persian architecture">Persian architecture</a>. One famous example was a large silver tree with cleverly designed pipes that dispensed various drinks. The tree, topped by a triumphant angel, was crafted by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Guillaume_Boucher&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Guillaume Boucher (page does not exist)">Guillaume Boucher</a>, a Parisian goldsmith.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hulagu_Khan.jpg"><img alt="Stylized line drawing of Hulagu, seated and drinking from a bowl" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1241" data-file-width="830" height="329" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Hulagu_Khan.jpg/220px-Hulagu_Khan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Hulagu_Khan.jpg/330px-Hulagu_Khan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Hulagu_Khan.jpg/440px-Hulagu_Khan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hulagu_Khan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hulagu" title="Hulagu">Hulagu</a>, Genghis Khan's grandson and founder of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Il-Khanate" title="Il-Khanate">Il-Khanate</a>. From a medieval Persian manuscript.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although he had a strong Chinese contingent, Möngke relied heavily on Muslim and Mongol administrators and launched a series of economic reforms to make government expenses more predictable. His court limited government spending and prohibited nobles and troops from abusing civilians or issuing edicts without authorization. He commuted the contribution system into a fixed poll tax that was collected by imperial agents and forwarded to units in need.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allsen._p._280_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Allsen._p._280-71">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>His court also tried to lighten the tax burden on commoners by reducing tax rates. Along with the reform of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tax_system" title="Tax system">tax system</a>, he reinforced the guards at the postal relays and centralized control of monetary affairs. Möngke also ordered an empire-wide census in 1252 that took several years to complete, not finished until <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Novgorod" title="Novgorod">Novgorod</a> in the far northwest was counted in 1258.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allsen._p._280_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-Allsen._p._280-71">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>In another move to consolidate his power, Möngke assigned his brothers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hulagu" title="Hulagu">Hulagu</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kublai" title="Kublai">Kublai</a> to rule Persia and Mongol-held China. In the southern part of the empire, he continued his predecessors' struggle against the <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a>. In order to outflank the Song from three directions, Möngke dispatched Mongol armies under his brother Kublai to <a href="/wiki/Yunnan" title="Yunnan">Yunnan</a>, and under his uncle Iyeku to subdue Korea and pressure the Song from that direction as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atwood-255_64-3"><a href="#cite_note-atwood-255-64">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kublai conquered the <a href="/wiki/Dali_Kingdom" title="Dali Kingdom">Dali Kingdom</a> in 1253 after the Dali King Duan Xingzhi defected to the Mongols and helped them conquer the rest of Yunnan, and Möngke's general Qoridai stabilized his control over Tibet, inducing leading monasteries to submit to Mongol rule. Subutai's son Uryankhadai reduced the neighboring peoples of Yunnan to submission and defeated the <a href="/wiki/Tr%E1%BA%A7n_dynasty" title="Trần dynasty">Trần dynasty</a> in northern Vietnam in 1257, but they had to draw back in 1258.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atwood-255_64-4"><a href="#cite_note-atwood-255-64">[61]</a></sup> The Mongol Empire tried to invade Vietnam again in 1284 and 1287 but were defeated both times.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_invasions_of_the_Middle_East_and_Southern_China">New invasions of the Middle East and Southern China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: New invasions of the Middle East and Southern China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_the_Levant" title="Mongol invasions of the Levant">Mongol invasions of the Levant</a></div>
