<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2786" data-file-width="4429" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg/220px-DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg/330px-DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg/440px-DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mongol invasion of Baghdad</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After stabilizing the empire's finances, Möngke once again sought to expand its borders. At kurultais in Karakorum in 1253 and 1258 he approved new invasions of the Middle East and <a href="/wiki/South_Central_China" title="South Central China">south China</a>. Möngke put Hulagu in overall charge of military and civil affairs in Persia, and appointed Chagataids and Jochids to join Hulagu's army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._129_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._129-72">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Muslims from <a href="/wiki/Qazvin" title="Qazvin">Qazvin</a> denounced the menace of the <a href="/wiki/Nizari" title="Nizari">Nizari</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ismailis" title="Ismailis">Ismailis</a>, a heretical sect of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shiites" title="Shiites">Shiites</a>. The Mongol Naiman commander <a href="/wiki/Kitbuqa" title="Kitbuqa">Kitbuqa</a> began to assault several Ismaili fortresses in 1253, before Hulagu deliberately advanced in 1256. Ismaili Grand Master <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rukn_ud-Din&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rukn ud-Din (page does not exist)">Rukn ud-Din</a> surrendered in 1257 and was executed. All of the Ismaili strongholds in Persia were destroyed by Hulagu's army in 1257, though Girdukh held out until 1271.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._129_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._129-72">[69]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bagdad1258.jpg"><img alt="Colorful medieval depiction of a siege, showing the city of Baghdad surrounded by walls, and the Mongol army outside" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="567" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bagdad1258.jpg/220px-Bagdad1258.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bagdad1258.jpg/330px-Bagdad1258.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bagdad1258.jpg/440px-Bagdad1258.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bagdad1258.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad_(1258)" title="Siege of Baghdad (1258)">Fall of Baghdad, 1258</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The center of the Islamic Empire at the time was Baghdad, which had held power for 500 years but was suffering internal divisions. When its caliph <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Mustasim" title="Al-Mustasim">al-Mustasim</a> refused to submit to the Mongols, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Baghdad_(1258)" title="Battle of Baghdad (1258)">Baghdad was besieged and captured</a> by the Mongols in 1258, an event considered as one of the more catastrophic events in the history of Islam, and sometimes compared to the rupture of the <a href="/wiki/Kaaba" title="Kaaba">Kaaba</a>. With the destruction of the Abbasid Caliphate, Hulagu had an open route to Syria and moved against the other Muslim powers in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._pp._132_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._pp._132-73">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>His army advanced towards <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ayyubid" title="Ayyubid">Ayyubid</a>-ruled Syria, capturing small local states en route. The sultan <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Nasir_Yusuf" title="Al-Nasir Yusuf">Al-Nasir Yusuf</a> of the Ayyubids refused to show himself before Hulagu; however, he had accepted Mongol supremacy two decades earlier. When Hulagu headed further west, the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Armenia" title="Lesser Armenia">Armenians</a> from <a href="/wiki/Cilicia" title="Cilicia">Cilicia</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seljuks" title="Seljuks">Seljuks</a> from <a href="/wiki/Rum" title="Rum">Rum</a> and the Christian realms of <a href="/wiki/Antioch" title="Antioch">Antioch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a> submitted to Mongol authority, joining the Mongols in their assault against the Muslims. While some cities surrendered without resisting, others such as Mayafarriqin fought back; their populations were massacred and the cities were sacked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._pp._132_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._pp._132-73">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_M.C3.B6ngke_Khan_.281259.29">Death of Möngke Khan (1259)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Death of Möngke Khan (1259)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MongolEmpire.jpg"><img alt="Map of Asia" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="366" data-file-width="700" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/MongolEmpire.jpg/220px-MongolEmpire.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/MongolEmpire.jpg/330px-MongolEmpire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/MongolEmpire.jpg/440px-MongolEmpire.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MongolEmpire.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The extent of the Mongol Empire after the death of <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6ngke_Khan" title="Möngke Khan">Möngke Khan</a> (reigned 1251–59).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Meanwhile, in the northwestern portion of the empire, Batu's successor and younger brother <a href="/wiki/Berke" title="Berke">Berke</a> sent punitive expeditions to Ukraine, Belarus, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, and Poland. Dissension began brewing between the northwestern and southwestern sections of the Mongol Empire as Batu suspected that Hulagu's invasion of Western Asia would result in the elimination of Batu's own predominance there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the southern part of the empire, Möngke Khan himself led his army to complete the conquest of China. Military operations were generally successful, but prolonged, so the forces did not withdraw to the north as was customary when the weather turned hot. Disease ravaged the Mongol forces with bloody epidemics, and Möngke died there on August 11, 1259. This event began a new chapter of history for the Mongols, as again a decision needed to be made on a new great khan. Mongol armies across the empire withdrew from their campaigns to once again convene for a new kurultai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disunity">Disunity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Disunity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dispute_over_succession">Dispute over succession</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Dispute over succession">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1150" data-file-width="1648" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg/220px-DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg/330px-DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg/440px-DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Mongols at war</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Möngke's brother Hulagu broke off his successful military advance into Syria, withdrawing the bulk of his forces to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mughan" title="Mughan">Mughan</a> and leaving only a small contingent under his general <a href="/wiki/Kitbuqa" title="Kitbuqa">Kitbuqa</a>. The opposing forces in the region, the Christian Crusaders and Muslim Mamluks, both recognizing that the Mongols were the greater threat, took advantage of the weakened state of the Mongol army and engaged in an unusual passive truce with each other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._138_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._138-76">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1260, the Mamluks advanced from Egypt, being allowed to camp and resupply near the Christian stronghold of <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a>, and engaged Kitbuqa's forces just north of Galilee at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ain_Jalut" title="Battle of Ain Jalut">Battle of Ain Jalut</a>. The Mongols were defeated, and Kitbuqa executed. This pivotal battle marked the western limit for Mongol expansion, and the Mongols were never again able to make any serious military advances farther than Syria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._138_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._138-76">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a separate part of the empire, <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a>, another brother of Hulagu and Möngke, heard of the great khan's death at the Huai River in China. Rather than returning to the capital, he continued his advance into the <a href="/wiki/Wuchang_District" title="Wuchang District">Wuchang</a> area of China, near the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a>. Their younger brother <a href="/wiki/Ariq_B%C3%B6ke" title="Ariq Böke">Ariqboke</a> took advantage of the absence of Hulagu and Kublai, and used his position at the capital to win the title of great khan for himself, with representatives of all the family branches proclaiming him as the leader at the kurultai in Karakorum. When Kublai learned of this, he summoned his own kurultai at <a href="/wiki/Kaiping" title="Kaiping">Kaiping</a>, and nearly all the senior princes and great noyans in North China and Manchuria supported his own candidacy over that of Ariqboke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._p._104_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._p._104-59">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mongolian_Civil_War">Mongolian Civil War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Mongolian Civil War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Toluid_Civil_War" title="Toluid Civil War">Toluid Civil War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berke%E2%80%93Hulagu_war" title="Berke–Hulagu war">Berke–Hulagu war</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1339" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg/220px-YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg/330px-YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg/440px-YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a>'s grandson and founder of the Yuan dynasty</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Battles ensued between the armies of Kublai and those of his brother Ariqboke, which included forces still loyal to Möngke's previous administration. Kublai's army easily eliminated Ariqboke's supporters and seized control of the civil administration in southern Mongolia. Further challenges took place from their cousins, the Chagataids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wassaf_p._12_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wassaf_p._12-77">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson._p._109_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson._p._109-78">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barthold._Turkestan._p._488_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barthold._Turkestan._p._488-79">[76]</a></sup> Kublai sent Abishka, a Chagataid prince loyal to him, to take charge of Chagatai's realm. But Ariqboke captured and then executed Abishka, having his own man <a href="/wiki/Alghu" title="Alghu">Alghu</a> crowned there instead. Kublai's new administration blockaded Ariqboke in Mongolia to cut food supplies, causing a famine. Karakorum fell quickly to Kublai, but Ariqboke rallied and re-took the capital in 1261.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wassaf_p._12_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wassaf_p._12-77">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson._p._109_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson._p._109-78">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barthold._Turkestan._p._488_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barthold._Turkestan._p._488-79">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the southwestern Ilkhanate, Hulagu was loyal to his brother Kublai, but clashes with their cousin Berke, the ruler of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a> in the northwestern part of the empire, began in 1262. The suspicious deaths of Jochid princes in Hulagu's service, unequal distribution of war booty, and Hulagu's massacres of the Muslims increased the anger of Berke, who considered supporting a rebellion of the Georgian Kingdom against Hulagu's rule in 1259–1260.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[77]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A more detailed citation is required. (November 2012)">full citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Berke also forged an alliance with the Egyptian Mamluks against Hulagu and supported Kublai's rival claimant, Ariqboke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barthold_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-barthold-81">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hulagu died on February 8, 1264. Berke sought to take advantage and invade Hulagu's realm, but he died along the way, and a few months later Alghu Khan of the Chagatai Khanate died as well. Kublai named Hulagu's son <a href="/wiki/Abaqa_Khan" title="Abaqa Khan">Abaqa</a> as a new Ilkhan, and Abaqa sought foreign alliances, such as attempting to form a <a href="/wiki/Franco-Mongol_alliance" title="Franco-Mongol alliance">Franco-Mongol alliance</a> with the Europeans against the Egyptian Mamluks. Kublai nominated Batu's grandson <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%B6ngke_Tem%C3%BCr" title="Möngke Temür">Möngke Temür</a> to lead the Golden Horde.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[79]</a></sup> Ariqboqe surrendered to Kublai at <a href="/wiki/Shangdu" title="Shangdu">Shangdu</a> on August 21, 1264.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Campaigns_of_Kublai_Khan_.281264.E2.80.931294.29">Campaigns of Kublai Khan (1264–1294)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Campaigns of Kublai Khan (1264–1294)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan%27s_Campaigns" title="Kublai Khan's Campaigns">Kublai Khan's Campaigns</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1461" data-file-width="3184" height="101" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg/220px-M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg/330px-M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg/440px-M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">samurai</a> <a href="/wiki/Takezaki_Suenaga" title="Takezaki Suenaga">Suenaga</a> facing Mongol arrows and bombs. <i><a href="/wiki/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba" title="Mōko Shūrai Ekotoba">Mōko Shūrai Ekotoba</a></i> (蒙古襲来絵詞), circa 1293.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the south, after <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Xiangyang" title="Battle of Xiangyang">the fall of Xiangyang</a> in 1273, the Mongols sought the final conquest of the Song dynasty in South China. In 1271, Kublai renamed the new Mongol regime in China as the <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a> and sought to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinicize" title="Sinicize">sinicize</a> his image as <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_China" title="Emperor of China">Emperor of China</a> to win the control of the Chinese people. Kublai moved his headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Khanbaliq" title="Khanbaliq">Dadu</a>, the genesis for what later became the modern city of <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, although his establishment of a capital there was a controversial move to many Mongols who accused him of being too closely tied to <a href="/wiki/Chinese_culture" title="Chinese culture">Chinese culture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Mongols were eventually successful in their campaigns against (Song) China, and the Chinese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Song" title="Southern Song">Song imperial family</a> surrendered to the Yuan in 1276, making the Mongols the first non-Chinese people to conquer all of China. Kublai used his base to build a powerful empire, creating an academy, offices, trade ports and canals, and sponsoring arts and science. Mongol records list 20,166 public schools created during his reign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-man_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-man-86">[83]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mongol_warrior_of_Genghis_Khan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="760" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Mongol_warrior_of_Genghis_Khan.jpg/220px-Mongol_warrior_of_Genghis_Khan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Mongol_warrior_of_Genghis_Khan.jpg/330px-Mongol_warrior_of_Genghis_Khan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Mongol_warrior_of_Genghis_Khan.jpg/440px-Mongol_warrior_of_Genghis_Khan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mongol_warrior_of_Genghis_Khan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mongol warrior on horseback, preparing a mounted archery shot.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After achieving actual or nominal dominion over much of Eurasia and successfully conquering China, Kublai pursued further expansion. His <a href="/wiki/First_Mongol_invasion_of_Burma" title="First Mongol invasion of Burma">invasions of Burma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a> were costly, and his <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Vietnam" title="Mongol invasions of Vietnam">attempted invasions</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Annam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Champa" title="Champa">Champa</a> ended in devastating defeat, but secured vassal statuses of those countries. The Mongol armies were massacred and smashed repeatedly in Annam and at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_B%E1%BA%A1ch_%C4%90%E1%BA%B1ng_(1288)" title="Battle of Bạch Đằng (1288)">Battle of Bạch Đằng (1288)</a>. Annam (Vietnam) was ruled by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tran_dynasty" title="Tran dynasty">Tran dynasty</a>. The Chinese region of <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a> was the original home of the Chinese Tran (Chen) clan before they migrated under Trần Kinh (陳京, Chén Jīng) to Dai Viet and whose descendants established the Trần dynasty which ruled Vietnam Đại Việt, and certain members of the clan could still speak Chinese when a Yuan dynasty envoy had a meeting with the Chinese-speaking Trần prince Trần Quốc Tuấn (later King <a href="/wiki/Tr%E1%BA%A7n_H%C6%B0ng_%C4%90%E1%BA%A1o" title="Trần Hưng Đạo">Trần Hưng Đạo</a>) in 1282.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taylor2013_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor2013-87">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall2008_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hall2008-88">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WernerWhitmore2012_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-WernerWhitmore2012-89">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gunn2011_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gunn2011-90">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EmbreeLewis1988_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-EmbreeLewis1988-91">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Woodside1971_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Woodside1971-92">[89]</a></sup> However, further <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Japan" title="Mongol invasion of Japan">Mongol invasions of Japan</a> in 1274 and 1280, and of <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Java" title="Mongol invasion of Java">Java</a> in 1293 failed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-man_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-man-86">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nogai and <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ch%C3%BC" title="Köchü">Konchi</a>, the khan of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Horde" title="White Horde">White Horde</a>, established friendly relations with the Yuan dynasty and the Ilkhanate. Political disagreement among contending branches of the family over the office of great khan continued, but the economic and commercial success of the Mongol Empire continued despite the squabbling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disintegration_into_competing_entities">Disintegration into competing entities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Disintegration into competing entities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Division_of_the_Mongol_Empire" title="Division of the Mongol Empire">Division of the Mongol Empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fun%C3%A9railles_de_Tchaghata%C3%AF.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="390" data-file-width="399" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Fun%C3%A9railles_de_Tchaghata%C3%AF.jpeg/220px-Fun%C3%A9railles_de_Tchaghata%C3%AF.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Fun%C3%A9railles_de_Tchaghata%C3%AF.jpeg/330px-Fun%C3%A9railles_de_Tchaghata%C3%AF.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/87/Fun%C3%A9railles_de_Tchaghata%C3%AF.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fun%C3%A9railles_de_Tchaghata%C3%AF.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The funeral of <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khan" title="Chagatai Khan">Chagatai Khan</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Major changes occurred in the Mongol Empire in the late 1200s. Kublai Khan, after having conquered all of China and established the Yuan dynasty, died in 1294, and was succeeded by his grandson <a href="/wiki/Tem%C3%BCr_Khan" title="Temür Khan">Temür Khan</a>, who continued Kublai's policies. At the same time, the <a href="/wiki/Toluid_Civil_War" title="Toluid Civil War">Toluid Civil War</a>, along with the <a href="/wiki/Berke%E2%80%93Hulagu_war" title="Berke–Hulagu war">Berke–Hulagu war</a> and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Kaidu%E2%80%93Kublai_war" title="Kaidu–Kublai war">Kaidu–Kublai war</a> greatly weakened the authority of the great khan over the entirety of the Mongol Empire and the empire fractured into autonomous khanates, including the Yuan dynasty and the three western khanates (the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khanate" title="Chagatai Khanate">Chagatai Khanate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ilkhanate" title="Ilkhanate">Ilkhanate</a>). All of them became functionally autonomous; only the Ilkhanate remained loyal to the Yuan court but endured its own power struggle, in part because of a dispute with the growing Islamic factions within the southwestern part of the empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-96">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the death of <a href="/wiki/Kaidu" title="Kaidu">Kaidu</a>, the Chatagai ruler Duwa initiated a peace proposal and persuaded the Ögedeids to submit to Temür Khan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[95]</a></sup> In 1304, all khanates approved a peace treaty and accepted Yuan emperor Temür's supremacy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[99]</a></sup> This established the nominal supremacy of the Yuan dynasty over the western khanates. While this supremacy based on nothing like the same foundations as that of the earlier Khagans (such as the continued border clashes among them) and each of the four khanates continued to develop separately and function as different states, the nominal supremacy did last for a few decades.</p>
<p>Nearly a century of conquest and civil war was followed by relative stability (<i><a href="/wiki/Pax_Mongolica" title="Pax Mongolica">Pax Mongolica</a></i>), and international trade and cultural exchanges flourished between Asia and Europe. Communication between the Yuan dynasty in China and Ilkhanate in Persia further encouraged trade and commerce between east and west. Patterns of Yuan royal textiles could be found on the opposite side of the empire adorning Armenian decorations; trees and vegetables were transplanted across the empire; and technological innovations spread from Mongol dominions towards the West.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[100]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_XXII" title="Pope John XXII">Pope John XXII</a> was presented a memorandum from the eastern church describing the Pax Mongolica: "... Khagan is one of the greatest monarchs and all lords of the state, e.g., the king of Almaligh (Chagatai Khanate), emperor Abu Said and Uzbek Khan, are his subjects, saluting his holiness to pay their respects."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[101]</a></sup> However, while the four khanates continued to interact with one another well into the 14th century, they did so as <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign states</a> and never again pooled their resources in a cooperative military endeavor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Developments_of_the_khanates">Developments of the khanates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Developments of the khanates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tem%C3%BCr_Chabar_Toqta_%C3%96ldje%C3%AFtu.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1181" data-file-width="1908" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Tem%C3%BCr_Chabar_Toqta_%C3%96ldje%C3%AFtu.jpeg/220px-Tem%C3%BCr_Chabar_Toqta_%C3%96ldje%C3%AFtu.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Tem%C3%BCr_Chabar_Toqta_%C3%96ldje%C3%AFtu.jpeg/330px-Tem%C3%BCr_Chabar_Toqta_%C3%96ldje%C3%AFtu.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Tem%C3%BCr_Chabar_Toqta_%C3%96ldje%C3%AFtu.jpeg/440px-Tem%C3%BCr_Chabar_Toqta_%C3%96ldje%C3%AFtu.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tem%C3%BCr_Chabar_Toqta_%C3%96ldje%C3%AFtu.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A European depiction of the four khans, Temür (Yuan), Chapar (<a href="/wiki/House_of_%C3%96gedei" title="House of Ögedei">House of Ögedei</a>), <a href="/wiki/Toqta" title="Toqta">Toqta</a> (Golden Horde), and Öljaitü (Ilkhanate), in the <i>Fleur des histoires d'orient</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[103]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In spite of his conflicts with Kaidu and Duwa, Yuan emperor Temür established a tributary relationship with the war-like <a href="/wiki/Shan_people" title="Shan people">Shan</a> brothers after his series of military operations against <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> from 1297 to 1303. This was to mark the end of the southern expansion of the Mongols.</p>
<p>When <a href="/wiki/Ghazan" title="Ghazan">Ghazan</a> took the throne of the Ilkhanate in 1295, he formally accepted Islam as his own religion, marking a turning point in Mongol history after which Mongol Persia became more and more Islamic. Despite this though, Ghazan continued to strengthen ties with Temür Khan and the Yuan dynasty in the east. It was politically useful to advertise the great khan's authority in the Ilkhanate, because the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a> in Russia had long made claims on nearby Georgia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-96">[93]</a></sup> Within four years, Ghazan began sending tributes to the Yuan court and appealing to other khans to accept Temür Khan as their overlord. He oversaw an extensive program of cultural and scientific interaction between the Ilkhanate and the Yuan dynasty in the following decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ghazan's faith may have been Islamic, but he continued his ancestors' war with the Egyptian Mamluks, and consulted with his old Mongolian advisers in his native tongue. He defeated the Mamluk army at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wadi_al-Khazandar" title="Battle of Wadi al-Khazandar">Battle of Wadi al-Khazandar</a> in 1299, but he was only briefly able to occupy Syria, due to distracting raids from the <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khanate" title="Chagatai Khanate">Chagatai Khanate</a> under its <i>de facto</i> ruler <a href="/wiki/Kaidu" title="Kaidu">Kaidu</a>, who was <a href="/wiki/Kaidu%E2%80%93Kublai_war" title="Kaidu–Kublai war">at war</a> with both the Ilkhans and the Yuan dynasty.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Struggling for influence within the Golden Horde, Kaidu sponsored his own candidate Kobeleg against <a href="/wiki/Bayan_(khan)" title="Bayan (khan)">Bayan</a> (r. 1299–1304), the khan of the White Horde. Bayan, after receiving military support from the Mongols in Russia, requested assistance from both Temür Khan and the Ilkhanate to organize a unified attack against Kaidu's forces. Temür was amenable and enlarged counterattacks against Kaidu a year later. After a bloody battle with Temür's armies near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zawkhan_River" title="Zawkhan River">Zawkhan River</a> in 1301, the old valiant Kaidu died and was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Duwa" title="Duwa">Duwa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[106]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MongolsInHungary1241.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="505" data-file-width="741" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/MongolsInHungary1241.jpg/220px-MongolsInHungary1241.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/MongolsInHungary1241.jpg/330px-MongolsInHungary1241.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/MongolsInHungary1241.jpg/440px-MongolsInHungary1241.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MongolsInHungary1241.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hungarian King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B%C3%A9la_IV" title="Béla IV">Béla IV</a> in flight from the Mongols under general <a href="/wiki/Kadan" title="Kadan">Kadan</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Duwa was challenged by Kaidu's son Chapar, but with the assistance of Temür, Duwa defeated the Ögedeids. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tokhta" title="Tokhta">Tokhta</a> of the Golden Horde, also seeking a general peace, sent 20,000 men to buttress the Yuan frontier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[107]</a></sup> Tokhta died in 1312, though, and was succeeded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ozbeg" title="Ozbeg">Ozbeg</a> (r. 1313–41), who seized the throne of the Golden Horde and persecuted non-Muslim Mongols. The Yuan's influence on the Horde was largely reversed and border clashes between Mongol states resumed. <a href="/wiki/Ayurbarwada_Buyantu_Khan" title="Ayurbarwada Buyantu Khan">Ayurbarwada Buyantu Khan</a>'s envoys backed Tokhta's son against Ozbeg.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In the Chagatai Khanate, <a href="/wiki/Esen_Buqa_I" title="Esen Buqa I">Esen Buqa I</a> (r. 1309-1318) was enthroned as khan after suppressing a sudden rebellion by Ögedei's descendants and driving Chapar into exile. The Yuan and Ilkhanid armies eventually attacked the Chagatai Khanate. Realizing economic benefits and the Genghisid legacy, Ozbeg reopened friendly relations with the Yuan in 1326, and strengthened ties with the Muslim world as well, building mosques and other elaborate places such as baths.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> By the second decade of the 14th century, Mongol invasions had further decreased. In 1323, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abu_Sa%27id_(Ilkhanid_dynasty)" title="Abu Sa'id (Ilkhanid dynasty)">Abu Said Khan</a> (r. 1316-35) of the Ilkhanate signed a peace treaty with Egypt. At his request, the Yuan court awarded his custodian <a href="/wiki/Chupan" title="Chupan">Chupan</a> the title of commander-in-chief of all Mongol khanates, but Chupan died in late 1327.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Civil_war" title="Civil war">Civil war</a> erupted in the Yuan dynasty in 1328–29. After the death of Yesün Temür in 1328, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tugh_Tem%C3%BCr" title="Tugh Temür">Tugh Temür</a> became the new leader in Dadu, while Yesün Temür's son <a href="/wiki/Ragibagh_Khan" title="Ragibagh Khan">Ragibagh</a> succeeded to the throne in Shangdu, leading to the civil war known as the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Two_Capitals" title="War of the Two Capitals">War of the Two Capitals</a>. Tugh Temür defeated Ragibagh, but the Chagatai khan <a href="/wiki/Eljigidey" title="Eljigidey">Eljigidey</a> (r. 1326–29) supported <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kusala" title="Kusala">Kusala</a>, elder brother of Tugh Temür, as great khan. He invaded with a commanding force, and Tugh Temür abdicated. Kusala was elected khan on August 30, 1329. Kusala was then poisoned by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kypchak" title="Kypchak">Kypchak</a> commander under Tugh Temür, who returned to power. Tugh Temür (1304–32) was knowledgeable about Chinese language and history and was also a creditable poet, calligrapher, and painter. In order to be accepted by other khanates as the sovereign of the Mongol world, he sent Genghisid princes and descendants of other notable Mongol generals to the Chagatai Khanate, Ilkhan Abu Said, and Ozbeg. In response to the emissaries, they all agreed to send tribute each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[109]</a></sup> Furthermore, Tugh Temür gave lavish presents and an imperial seal to Eljigidey to mollify his anger.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relict_states_of_the_Mongol_Empire">Relict states of the Mongol Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Relict states of the Mongol Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MongolEmpireDivisions1300.png"><img alt="Map of Asia" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="959" data-file-width="1644" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/MongolEmpireDivisions1300.png/250px-MongolEmpireDivisions1300.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/MongolEmpireDivisions1300.png/375px-MongolEmpireDivisions1300.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/MongolEmpireDivisions1300.png/500px-MongolEmpireDivisions1300.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MongolEmpireDivisions1300.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The relict states of the Mongol Empire by 1300.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With the death of Ilkhan <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abu_Sa%27id_(Ilkhanid_dynasty)" title="Abu Sa'id (Ilkhanid dynasty)">Abu Said Bahatur</a> in 1335, Mongol rule faltered and Persia fell into political anarchy. A year later his successor was killed by an Oirat governor, and the Ilkhanate was divided between the Suldus, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jalayir" title="Jalayir">Jalayir</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J%C3%B6chi_Khasar" title="Jöchi Khasar">Qasarid</a> <a href="/wiki/Togha_Tem%C3%BCr" title="Togha Temür">Togha Temür</a> (d. 1353), and Persian warlords. Taking advantage of the chaos, the Georgians pushed the Mongols out of their own territory, and the Uyghur commander <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ghiyath_al-Din_Eretna&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ghiyath al-Din Eretna (page does not exist)">Eretna</a> established an independent state (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ertenids&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ertenids (page does not exist)">Ertenids</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> in 1336. Following the downfall of their Mongol masters, the loyal vassal, the Armenian Kingdom of Cilicia, received escalating threats from the Mamluks and were eventually overrun.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Along with the dissolution of the Ilkhanate in Persia, Mongol rulers in China and the <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khanate" title="Chagatai Khanate">Chagatai Khanate</a> were also in turmoil. The plague known as the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a>, which started in the Mongol dominions and spread to Europe, added to the confusion. Disease devastated all the khanates, cutting off commercial ties and killing millions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[110]</a></sup> Plague may have taken 50 million lives in Europe alone in the 14th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[111]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D0%BD%D1%8F%D0%B7%D1%8C_%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BE_%D0%9E%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%83_%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B2%D1%96_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%96%D1%85_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%85.1362_%D1%80%D1%96%D0%BA.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1240" data-file-width="2110" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/%D0%9A%D0%BD%D1%8F%D0%B7%D1%8C_%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BE_%D0%9E%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%83_%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B2%D1%96_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%96%D1%85_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%85.1362_%D1%80%D1%96%D0%BA.jpg/220px-%D0%9A%D0%BD%D1%8F%D0%B7%D1%8C_%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BE_%D0%9E%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%83_%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B2%D1%96_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%96%D1%85_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%85.1362_%D1%80%D1%96%D0%BA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/%D0%9A%D0%BD%D1%8F%D0%B7%D1%8C_%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BE_%D0%9E%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%83_%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B2%D1%96_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%96%D1%85_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%85.1362_%D1%80%D1%96%D0%BA.jpg/330px-%D0%9A%D0%BD%D1%8F%D0%B7%D1%8C_%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BE_%D0%9E%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%83_%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B2%D1%96_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%96%D1%85_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%85.1362_%D1%80%D1%96%D0%BA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/%D0%9A%D0%BD%D1%8F%D0%B7%D1%8C_%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BE_%D0%9E%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%83_%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B2%D1%96_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%96%D1%85_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%85.1362_%D1%80%D1%96%D0%BA.jpg/440px-%D0%9A%D0%BD%D1%8F%D0%B7%D1%8C_%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BE_%D0%9E%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%83_%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B2%D1%96_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%96%D1%85_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%85.1362_%D1%80%D1%96%D0%BA.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D0%BD%D1%8F%D0%B7%D1%8C_%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BE_%D0%9E%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B7%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%83_%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B2%D1%96_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%96%D1%85_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%85.1362_%D1%80%D1%96%D0%BA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Blue_Waters" title="Battle of Blue Waters">Battle of Blue Waters</a> between the armies of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Lithuania</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a> in 1362</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As the power of the Mongols declined, chaos erupted throughout the empire as non-Mongol leaders expanded their own influence. The <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a> lost all of its western dominions (including modern <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>) to Poland and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> from 1342 to 1369. Muslim and non-Muslim princes in the Chagatai Khanate warred with each other from 1331–43, and the Chagatai Khanate disintegrated when non-Genghisid warlords set up their own puppet khans in <a href="/wiki/Transoxiana" title="Transoxiana">Transoxiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moghulistan" title="Moghulistan">Moghulistan</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Janibeg" title="Janibeg">Janibeg</a> Khan (r. 1342–1357) briefly reasserted Jochid dominance over the Chaghataids to restore their former glory. Demanding submission from an offshoot of the Ilkhanate in <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, he boasted that "today three uluses are under my control".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prawdin._p._379_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Prawdin._p._379-115">[112]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:116px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Menli_I_Giray.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="196" data-file-width="114" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/84/Menli_I_Giray.jpg" width="114"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Menli_I_Giray.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean" title="Crimean">Crimean</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tatar" title="Tatar">Tatar</a> <a href="/wiki/Khan_(title)" title="Khan (title)">khan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mengli_Giray" title="Mengli Giray">Mengli Giray</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>However, rival families of the Jochids began fighting for the throne of the Golden Horde after the assassination of his successor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berdibek" title="Berdibek">Berdibek</a> Khan in 1359. The last Yuan ruler <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toghan_Tem%C3%BCr" title="Toghan Temür">Toghan Temür</a> (r. 1333–70) was powerless to regulate those troubles because the empire had nearly reached its end. His court's unbacked currency had entered a <a href="/wiki/Hyperinflation" title="Hyperinflation">hyperinflationary</a> spiral and <a href="/wiki/Red_Turban_Rebellion" title="Red Turban Rebellion">the Han-Chinese people revolted</a> due to the Yuan's harsh restrictions. In the 1350s <a href="/wiki/Gongmin_of_Goryeo" title="Gongmin of Goryeo">Gongmin of Goryeo</a> successfully pushed Mongolian garrisons back and exterminated the family of Toghan Temür Khan's empress while <a href="/wiki/Tai_Situ_Changchub_Gyaltsen" title="Tai Situ Changchub Gyaltsen">Tai Situ Changchub Gyaltsen</a> managed to eliminate the Mongol influence in Tibet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prawdin._p._379_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-Prawdin._p._379-115">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>Increasingly isolated from their subjects, the Mongols quickly lost most of China to the rebellious <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming forces</a> in 1368 and fled to their homeland Mongolia. After the overthrow of the <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a>, the Golden Horde lost touch with Mongolia and China, while the two main parts of the Chagatai Khanate were defeated by <a href="/wiki/Timur" title="Timur">Timur</a> (Tamerlane) (1336–1405), who founded the <a href="/wiki/Timurid_Empire" title="Timurid Empire">Timurid Empire</a>. However, remnants of the Chagatai Khanate survived; the last Chagataid state to survive was the <a href="/wiki/Yarkent_Khanate" title="Yarkent Khanate">Yarkent Khanate</a>, until its defeat by the Oirat <a href="/wiki/Dzungar_Khanate" title="Dzungar Khanate">Dzungar Khanate</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Dzungar_conquest_of_Altishahr" title="Dzungar conquest of Altishahr">Dzungar conquest of Altishahr</a> in 1680. The Golden Horde broke into smaller Turkic-hordes that declined steadily in power through four long centuries. Among them, the khanate's shadow <a href="/wiki/Great_Horde" title="Great Horde">Great Horde</a> survived until 1502, when one of its successors, the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Crimean Khanate</a>, sacked Sarai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Halperin._p._28_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-Halperin._p._28-116">[113]</a></sup> The Crimean Khanate lasted until 1783, whereas khanates such as the <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Bukhara" title="Khanate of Bukhara">Khanate of Bukhara</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_Khanate" title="Kazakh Khanate">Kazakh Khanate</a> lasted even longer.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_organization">Military organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Military organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_military_tactics_and_organization" title="Mongol military tactics and organization">Mongol military tactics and organization</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Genghis_Khan_The_Exhibition_(5465078899).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="949" data-file-width="1430" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Genghis_Khan_The_Exhibition_%285465078899%29.jpg/220px-Genghis_Khan_The_Exhibition_%285465078899%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Genghis_Khan_The_Exhibition_%285465078899%29.jpg/330px-Genghis_Khan_The_Exhibition_%285465078899%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Genghis_Khan_The_Exhibition_%285465078899%29.jpg/440px-Genghis_Khan_The_Exhibition_%285465078899%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Genghis_Khan_The_Exhibition_(5465078899).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Reconstruction of a Mongol warrior</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The number of troops mustered by the Mongols is the subject of some scholarly debate,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[114]</a></sup> but was at least 105,000 in 1206.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[115]</a></sup> The Mongol military organization was simple but effective, based on the <a href="/wiki/Decimal" title="Decimal">decimal</a> system. The army was built up from squads of ten men each, arbans (10 people), zuuns (100), <a href="/wiki/Mingghan" title="Mingghan">Mingghans</a> (1000), and <a href="/wiki/Tumen_(unit)" title="Tumen (unit)">tumens</a> (10,000).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._pp._80_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._pp._80-119">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Mongols were most famous for their <a href="/wiki/Mounted_archery" title="Mounted archery">horse archers</a>, but troops armed with lances were equally skilled, and the Mongols recruited other military talents from the cities they conquered. With experienced Chinese engineers and bombardier corps who were experts in building <a href="/wiki/Trebuchet" title="Trebuchet">trebuchets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Xiangyang" title="Battle of Xiangyang">Xuanfeng</a> catapults and other machines, the Mongols could lay siege to fortified positions, sometimes building machinery on the spot using available local resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._pp._80_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._pp._80-119">[116]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Subudei.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="600" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Subudei.jpg/220px-Subudei.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Subudei.jpg/330px-Subudei.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Subudei.jpg/440px-Subudei.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Subudei.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mongol general <a href="/wiki/Subutai" title="Subutai">Subutai</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Forces under the command of the Mongol Empire were trained, organized, and equipped for mobility and speed. Mongol soldiers were more lightly armored than many of the armies they faced but were able to make up for it with maneuverability. Each Mongol warrior would usually travel with multiple horses, allowing him to quickly switch to a fresh mount as needed. In addition, soldiers of the Mongol army functioned independently of <a href="/wiki/Military_supply_chain_management" title="Military supply chain management">supply lines</a>, considerably speeding up army movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._pp._74.E2.80.9375_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._pp._74.E2.80.9375-120">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>Skillful use of couriers enabled these armies to maintain contact with each other and their leadership. Discipline was inculcated during a <i>nerge</i> (traditional hunt), as reported by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ata_al-Mulk_Juvayni" title="Ata al-Mulk Juvayni">Juvayni</a>. These hunts were distinctive from hunts in other cultures where they were the equivalent to small unit actions. Mongol forces would spread out in a line, surround an entire region, and then drive all of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_(food)" title="Game (food)">game</a> within that area together. The goal was to let none of the animals escape and to slaughter them all.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._pp._74.E2.80.9375_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._pp._74.E2.80.9375-120">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another advantage of the Mongols was their ability to traverse large distances, even in unusually cold winters; for instance, frozen rivers led them like highways to large urban centers on their banks. In addition to siege engineering, the Mongols were also adept at river-work, crossing the river <a href="/wiki/Saj%C3%B3" title="Sajó">Sajó</a> in spring flood conditions with thirty thousand cavalry soldiers in a single night during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mohi" title="Battle of Mohi">Battle of Mohi</a> (April 1241) to defeat the Hungarian king <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B%C3%A9la_IV" title="Béla IV">Béla IV</a>. Similarly, in the attack against the Muslim <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_II_of_Khwarezm" title="Muhammad II of Khwarezm">Khwarezmshah</a>, a flotilla of barges was used to prevent escape on the river.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Traditionally known for their prowess with ground forces, the Mongols rarely used <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">naval</a> power, with a few exceptions. In the 1260s and 1270s they used seapower while conquering the <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a> of China, though their attempts to mount seaborne campaigns against Japan were unsuccessful. Around the Eastern Mediterranean, their campaigns were almost exclusively land-based, with the seas controlled by the Crusader and Mamluk forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>All military campaigns were preceded by careful planning, reconnaissance, and gathering sensitive information relating to enemy territories and forces. The success, organization, and mobility of the Mongol armies permitted them to fight on several fronts at once. All adult males up to the age of 60 were eligible for conscription into the army, a source of honor in their tribal warrior tradition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Society_of_the_Mongol_Empire" title="Society of the Mongol Empire">Society of the Mongol Empire</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_governance">Law and governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Law and governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_the_Mongol_Empire_under_Genghis_Khan" title="Organization of the Mongol Empire under Genghis Khan">Organization of the Mongol Empire under Genghis Khan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DiezAlbumsExecution.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1154" data-file-width="1659" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/DiezAlbumsExecution.jpg/220px-DiezAlbumsExecution.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/DiezAlbumsExecution.jpg/330px-DiezAlbumsExecution.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/DiezAlbumsExecution.jpg/440px-DiezAlbumsExecution.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DiezAlbumsExecution.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The executed - long and full beard probably means he is not a Mongol - has been thrown off a cliff.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Mongol Empire was governed by a code of law devised by Genghis, called <i><a href="/wiki/Yassa" title="Yassa">Yassa</a></i>, meaning "order" or "decree". A particular canon of this code was that those of rank shared much of the same hardship as the common man. It also imposed severe penalties — e.g., the death penalty was decreed if one mounted soldier following another did not pick up something dropped from the mount in front. Penalties were also decreed for rape and to some extent for murder. Any resistance to Mongol rule was met with massive collective punishment. Cities were destroyed and their inhabitants slaughtered if they defied Mongol orders.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On the whole, the tight discipline made the Mongol Empire extremely safe and well-run.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Under <i>Yassa</i>, chiefs and generals were selected based on <a href="/wiki/Meritocracy" title="Meritocracy">merit</a>. The empire was governed by a non-democratic, <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliamentary</a>-style central assembly, called <a href="/wiki/Kurultai" title="Kurultai">kurultai</a>, in which the Mongol chiefs met with the great khan to discuss domestic and foreign policies. Kurultais were also convened for the selection of each new great khan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[120]</a></sup> Throughout the empire, trade routes and an extensive postal system (<i>yam</i>) were created. Many merchants, messengers, and travelers from China, the Middle East, and Europe used the system. Genghis Khan also created a national seal, encouraged the use of a written alphabet in Mongolia, and exempted teachers, lawyers, and artists from taxes, although taxes were heavy on all other subjects of the empire.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>At the same time the Mongols imported Central Asian Muslims to serve as administrators in China, the Mongols also sent Han Chinese and Khitans from China to serve as administrators over the Muslim population in Bukhara in Central Asia, using foreigners to curtail the power of the local peoples of both lands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[121]</a></sup> The Mongols were very tolerant of other religions, and never persecuted people on religious grounds. This was associated with their culture and progressive thought. Some historians of the 20th century thought this was a good military strategy: when Genghis was at war with Sultan Muhammad of Khwarezm, other Islamic leaders did not join the fight, as it was seen as a non-holy war between two individuals.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mongol_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Religions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Mongol_Empire" title="Religion in the Mongol Empire">Religion in the Mongol Empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GhazanConversionToIslam.JPG"><img alt="Painting of a stylized building, showing Ghazan kneeling and accepting conversion" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2009" data-file-width="1498" height="295" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/GhazanConversionToIslam.JPG/220px-GhazanConversionToIslam.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/GhazanConversionToIslam.JPG/330px-GhazanConversionToIslam.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/GhazanConversionToIslam.JPG/440px-GhazanConversionToIslam.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
